Since the modernization of Chile's port sector, which took place in 1981,
EMPORCHI has had a highly profitable operation in financial terms. The main
reason for this performance has been the considerable reduction in operating
costs resulting from the 562 reduction in its staff (from 3,193 employees in 1980
to 1,394  by end-1982) which took place as a result of the transferring of
stevedoring activities to private operators. During the period under review
(1982-90) EMPORCHI's working and operating ratios have averaged 36 and 54,
respectively, and its net income before tax has averaged US$16 million
(equivalent) p.a., or 332 of revenues. Since the entity, by law, is required to
pay income taxee equivalent to 502 of income and, in addition, to transfer its
full net income after tax to the national budget, EMPORCHI has remained an
important source of funds to the Government over the last decade. Furthermore,
income tax payments have averaged US$8 million (equivalent) p.a. during this
period, consistent with the 50S tax rate, but the annual income transfers to the
national budget, have averaged US$11 million , indicating that EMPORCHI in
addition to its net income after tax has transferred also part of its
depreciation reserves.
8.        EMPORCHI's actual balance sheets 1982-1990 also reflect the entity's
healthy financial position (Table 2). Despite the fact that EMPORCHI transfers
to the national budget its full net income (after tax), which constitute an
important portion of its cash availability, the entity has maintained good
liquidity ratios. During the last five years (1986-90) the current ratio (current
assets/current liabilities) has averaged 2.4. This situation is mainly the result



- 79 -
ANNEX 6
Page 4 of 6
of the entity's very low level of short-term debt with both banks and suppliers.
Its debt/equity ratio, measured as long-term debt divided by net equity, has
been very low, remaining below 2% during the last 9 years.
9.        Actual  income statements  covering the  1984-1990 period  for the
Valparaiso, San Antonio and San Vicente ports have been included, respectively,
as Tables 3, 4 and 5 respectively. All three ports show considerable improvement
in their financial performance over the last seven years due mainly to higher
traffic levels and lower costs. At Valparaiso, working and operating r,atios
improved from 87 and 135, respectively, in 1984, to 27 and. 38 in 1990.
Particularly striking has been the continuing cost reduction at this port, where
the average cost per employee has dropped by 42% between 1984 and 1990. San
Antornio's financial improvement over this period is also worth noting ( working
and operating ratios reached 24 and 47, respectively, in 1990) as, following a
dramatic drop in traffic in 1985 and 1986 in which its installations were badly
damaged by the 1985 earthquake, the port has now recovered old traffil: levels and
continued implementing, successfully, the staff rationalization program (the
average cost per employee has dropped by 38% between 1984 and 1990). Finally,
San Vicente's financial performance also improved considerably, with working and
operatirg ratios declining from 32 and 54, respectively, in 1984, to 19 and 32
in 1990. At this port, the improvement has been made possible mainly by a steady
growth in traffic, as except for 1990, traffic levels have increased by an
average of 13% p.a. between 1984 and 1989.
E. Future Financial Performance
10.       One of EMPORCHI's main objectives, would be to remain a financially
viable entity within a framework of market competition with the private sector.
It would pursue maximizing efficiency in operations by handling more
traffic with lower operating costs, under a tariff structure designed to promote
an efficient resource allocation in the port sector. EMPORCHI should generate
sufficient revenues to cover its operating expenses, debt service charges and a
fair contribution to its capital needs, which in no case should be lower than
its share of the Bank project. An analysis of EMPORCHI's consolidated projected
financial situation is presented in paragraphs 11 through 13 following. A brief
discussion cn the expected results of project ports (Valparaiso, San Antonio and
San Vicente) is presented in paragraph 14 of this annex. Attachment 1 to this
annex summarizes the main assumptions used in the financial projections.
11.       EMPORCHI's projected income statements  for the period 1991-2000 are
presented in Table 6 of this annex. EMPORCHI's operating results would remain
sound over the next decade; the average working ratio is expected to remain at
the 36 level, and the average operating ratio would improve (from an average of
54 in the 1982-1990 period) to 51 during the forecast period. This performance
would be made possible as a result of a projected 3.5% p.a. average i- rease in
traffic, and therefore in revenues, which would offset minor cost increases
expected under some expense categories.
12.       EMPORCHI's cash position (Table 7) should also remain healthy over the
forecast period. The entity would generate annual operating cash surpluses



- 80 -
ANNEX 6
Page 5 of 6
(revenues less operating expenses) increasing gradually from the equivalent of
US$29.0 million in 1991 to US$36.0 million in the year 2000. This internal cash
generation together with the depreciation reserves would place  EMPORCHI, after
meeting its tax obligations, in a very favorable position with regards to project
financing. During every year of the forecast (1991-2000), the entity would be
in a position to finance its full investment program, including both its share
of the Bank project (counterpart funds) which it would channel to MOP's budget
through the Ministry of Finance, and its own investment requirements.   In
addition, EMPORCHI would continue having surpluses, except for 1992-1993, to
transfer to the national budget on account of its profits or net income. Only
during the first two years of project execution (approximately 1992-1993), when
the bulk of the project investments are expected to materialize, EMPORCHI will
have to suspend the transfer of funds to the national budget on account of
profits.
13.       EMPORCHI's balance sheet situation (Table 8) over the next ten years
would also remain favorable. Since the enzity would continue to generate cash
surpluses it would make sure to retain the funds necessary to maintain a
reasonable current (liquidity) ratio pr4.or to transferring its available net
income to the national budget.   The debt/equity ratio would also remain
reasonable, even with the Bank loan, as it would never exceed 20Z.
14.       The projected financial statements for Valparaiso, San Antonio and San
Vicente are presented in Tables 9 through 17 of this annex. The three ports show
a similar performance pattern, in financial terms, throughout the forecast
period; all three of them will generate profits, increasing slightly each year,
with working and operating ratios remaining or improving gradually to reach, in
the year 2000, 29 and 38 respectively in Valparaiso, 24 and 43 in San Antonio and
13 and 28 in San Vicente. Valparaiso and San Vicente will generate sufficient
funds to finance from their own resources the investments planned for each port.
Although San Antonio's will also generate cash surpluses to contribute to
financing its investments, during 1992, 1993, 1995 and 1996 it will need to
borrow funds from other ports (mainly Valparaiso) to complete the amounts
required. In 1997, however, San Antonio will start with the repayment of these
loans, which should be completed by about the end of the forecast period.
15.       The forecast shows that no increases to tariff levels, in real terms,
would be required to meet the entity's financial needs. It has been agreed,
however, that a restructuring of the present tariff structure, to ensure that
tariffs are contributing to an efficient resource allocation in the port
subsector under an environment of market competition with the private sector,
will be carried out before the end of 1993. In addition, even though the entity's
past and projected financial situation undoubtedly reflect excellent operational
and financial management, it has been agreed with the Government at negotiations
to include the following financial covenants in the legal documents of the loan
in order to ensure continuity of present practices during the project period:
(a) during the forecast period (1991-2000), EMPORCHI will achieve working ratios
no higher than 46; and (ii) EMPORCHI will take all measures necessary to provide
for each fiscal year funds from internal sources equivalent to at least its share
of the total cost of EMPORCHI project components after meeting cash operating



- 81 -
ANNEX 6
Page 6 of 6
expenses, debt service requirements (including for the proposed loan), increases
in working capital and other significant cash outflows other than capital
expenditures.
F. Sensitivity of Financial Forecasts
16.       The projections assume that working costs would increase by 3.52 p.a.
in real terms during the forecast period. Even if these costs grew at twice this
rate, this would not affect the entity's capacity to carry out the project, given
the profitability of its operation. It would only marginally reduce the amounts
to be transferred to the national budget on account of profits. Revenue
projections are considered to be conservative as they assume a modest average
annual traffic growth of about 3.5%, as compared to the 6Z annual (average)
growth of the 1982-1990 period.

CHILE
TRANSPORT INFRASTRUCTURE PPOJECT
Maior Assumptions for Financial Proiections
A. General
1.        All financial figures in this report have been presented in mid- 1991
constant Ch$ (chilean pesos), and the exchange rate used was US$1 - Ch$350.00.
2.        The financial projections were made for EMPORCHI as a whole and also
for each project port separately, in order to evaluate each port's capacity to
finance its own investment needs.
B. Traffic. Tariffs and Revenues
2.         Traffic   figures used in preparing the financial projections are
those included in Annex 2 of this report. As stated in that annex, traffic
forecasts for Valparaiso and San Antonio were originally prepared by consultants
BERGER-INECON in 1986, and updated by EMPORCHI staff in March 1991, to reflect
traffic developments during the last four years. Traffic projections for San
Vicente port were prepared by INECON consultants in 1987 and updated by EMPORCHI
staff in June 1990. Traffic forecasts for the rest of the ports were prepared by
EWPORCHI's staff in March 1991.
3.        The present tariffs were used in projecting revenues by the main
revenue headings, that is, no changes were introduced either to the structure or
to the level of tariffs. Since all tariffs are expressed in US$ terms, they were
translated into local currency at the exchange rate of US$1 - Ch$ 350.00.
C.  Ooeratina Costs
4.        The total labor force was assumed to increase by an average of less
than 12 p.a., that is, at a much lower rate than traffic, which is estimated to
grow by 3.4Z. This is .'ue to the fact that, since EMPORCHI is not directly
envolved in cargo handling, labor costs are not directly related to traffic
activity.



- 100 -
AMNEX 6
Attachment I
Page 2 of 2
5.        Maintenance costs were assumed to grow at the historic rate.
6.        Depreciation was calculated by asset or group of assets at the rates
established in the existing Chilean legislation.
7.        Interest on 1 .ns correspond to interest payable by EMPORCHI on the
loan to be obtained from the Bank (no other loans have been included). The terms
of borrowing from the Wforld Bank were assumed to be 17 years with a five-year
grace period (on the principal). Although the loan would be at the standard
variable rate, the current rate (7.7X) was used for purposes of financing.
D. Main Balance Sheet Items
8.        Accounts receivable were forecast to be 102 of operating revenues.
9.        Accounts payable were forecast to be 1% of maintenance and labor
related (taxes) expenses.
10.       Investments assumed are those of the proposed project plus EMPORCHI's
own investment requirements (US$10-11 million annually), the latter consisting
mainly of minor rehabilitation works on existing infrastructure.
11.       Given that during the construction period San Antonio's internal cash
generation is not sufficient to fully cover its share of the project cost, it has
been assumed that this port borrows funds from other EMPORCHI ports (mainly
Valparaiso) which will be generating surpluses.   San Antonio, however,  is
expected to fully repay these internal loans by the end of the decade, with the
pick-up in traffic that is expected as the project works are completed. These
loans have been reflected in the balance sheets of Valparaiso (other assets), San
Antonio (other long-term liabilities), as well as in the consolidated statements
(with matching amounts under assets and liabilities).

CHILE
TRANSPORT INFRASTRUCTURE PROJECT
Technical Assistance and Training Program
I. Technical Assistance
A. Transport Studies
(i) Development and Implementation of a Port Tariff System
Background. Although current port efficiency is good, and will further
improve with the container-handling technology provided under the proposed
project, to cope with forecast port traffic generated by increasing
foreign trade, important investments will be needed in the near future to
augment port capacity. To create additional incentives for private sector
investments on a competitive basis, the Government considers vital the
introduction of a transparent port tariff system to promote wider
participation of the former, and ensure a rational use of the financial
resources that will be required in the port subsector. The study will be
based on the one prepared in 1988 to analyse Port Tariff Alternatives,
financed under the Bank Loan 2504-CH.
Obiectives. The main objectives of the study are to: (i) establish
methodology and standard procedures for periodically reviewing maximum
tariff levels for regulated port services; (ii) design control mechanisms
to ensure compliance with such tariff levels; and (iii) implement the
tariff regulation system at EMPORCHI's ports.
Scope.   The study should:  (i) analyse the overall port  sector and
regulatory framework, complement the base study, and identify services
that may need to be regulated; (ii) develop simulation models for the
ports of the system related to the objectives of the study along with
tariff control mechanisms; and (iii) assist EMPORCHI in the implementation
of the tariff system, including the resulting tariff levels.
Cost and Timing. The cost based on manpower estimates, exluding taxes ist
Consultants: 24 man-months x US$  4,500       US$ 10.'s 000
6 man-months x US$ 13,000      US$  7cO,000
Travel and related expenses                   US$  14,000
Total                                         USS 200.000
The tentative chronogram will be as follows:

-     Study Award                           December 1991
-     Completion of Study                   January - December 1992
-     Implementation of Approved

(ii) Port Access Facilities: Technical and Feasibility Studies
Backrround. The Government has prepared Transport Strategy studies for
Valparaiso and other cities. The proposed study would be addressed to the
specific problams affecting access to the ports of San Antonio,
Valparaiso, and San Vicente, engineering design fcr works required, and
their social and economic feasibility.
Objectives. The objective of the study is to improve the flow of port
traffic while alleviating urban congestion in the vicinity of the ports.
Scone. The studies would include, but not be limited to: (a)
identification of alternative improvements; (b) preliminary engineering;
(c) economic and social evaluation; (d) consideration of the activities
within the ports that may be either improved or simplified by transfering
some of them to locations outside the ports, for example fruit inspection
and containers' customs clearance; and (e) social impact, for example
relocation of city's business/homes. Detailed engineering would then be
prepared separately.
Cost and TiminR.  The cost bpsed on manpower estimates, exluding taxes is:

(iii) Ferrv Terminal at Puerto Montts  Technical and Feasibillhy Studies
Background.   The port of Puertc Montt is the main intermodal transfer
point for passengers and freigh1: coming from or going to X, XI, and XII
Regions by ferry. However, the present ferry terminal was not conceived
taking into account its relations with the o her modes of transportation.
This  fact,  and the  increasing  demnd  associated with  the economic
dev6lopment of the regions makes it necessary to find an integral solution
to the current problems.

(iv)  Inland N,l.timodal Terminal
Background.   In August 1986, a study financed under Loan 2297-CH was
issued by a consulting firm under the title, "Diagnoellic, Analysis and
Recommendations for the Development of a Multimodal   Corridor between
Santiago and the Ports of the Vth Region".    The main recommendations
supported the development of the corridor, siven the importance of the
container demand at Santiago and the fact that the ports of San Antonio
and Valparaiso are the major gateways for that kind of traffic. Special
emphasis was placed on the need to construct inland multimodal terminals
to efficiently handle containers, but the report recognized that the major
drawback was the requirement by customs to inspect all boxes inside the
po t area.
Qkj ctivs. The main objectives of the study are: (i) to diagnose the
maiz, limitations preventing the development of inlasnd multimodal
torminals; (ii) to recommend solutions to Lhese problemss (iii) to analyze
possible locatioLs of the terminals, market conditions,  and required
Government-financed infrastructure; (iii) to propose schemes for the
financing, administration, and operation of the terminal3; (iv) to prepare
bidding documents, including a regulation system, to requeet private
financing for the terminal; and (v) to recommend ways of controlling or
preventing possible monopolistic cases.

B. Institutional Studies
(iM Institutional Reorganization of the Infrastructure Sector
Backaround. The Government has already started (through consultants), the
first step of this study, which addresses specific institutional problems
affecting the whole infrastructure sector. The number of possible problem
areas is enormous, and the consultants are planning to submit a draft
report by October 1991 with the results of a diagnostic and preliminary
problem areas identification.
Obiectives. The main objectives of the study are to: (i) prepare a
diagnostic of the existing situation, including sectors such as
irrigation, surface, water and air transport, drinking water, sewage, and
urban; (ii) recommend institutional reforms to improve the management,
operation, and maintenance of the infrastructure sector; and (iii) prepare
draft legislation to support the changes.
Scone. The work will be carried out in two phases. The first one will
comprise a diagnostic of the current situation, including the legal and
institutional framework. The second phase consists of the execution of at
least the following specific studies: water management and uses,
environmental improvements, highway, water and air transport management,
improvement of all activities in the project cycle, budgetary procedures
and allocations, and institutional urban problems.
Cost and Timina.   The cost for the second phase based on manpower
estimates, excluding taxes, is:

(ii) Institutional Set-uD for Small-Scale Fishing Sector
Backaround. New fishing wharves to serve small-scale fishing activities
are at present requested by interested parties to DIRECTEMAR and DOP; if
accepted from safety and technical viewpoints, the request is sent to
MIDEPLAN to process the project. Once it is built by DOP, the wharf is
open to general use, and, in general, no organization assumes
responsibility for its operation, maintenance, and cost recovery.
Obiectives. The main objective is to analyze the legal and institutional
implications of establishing a system to evaluate properly, administer,
maintain and manage (including the collection of user charges), a fishing
wharf.
Scoge. The study would include, but not exclusively: (a) recommendations
on the screening process to select the works; (b) ways of administering
the wharf, for its operation and maintenance; (c) legal aspects involved
in transfering ownership; (d) preparation of related handbooks and
training program; (e) cost recovery through user charges; and (f)
methodology for economic evaluation.
Cost and Timing. The estimated cost, excluding taxes, is:

(iii) Fishing Facilities in the Vth Region
Background.   The accelerated economic growth of this Region and the
consequences of the 1985 earthquake have created different kinds of
problems for the fishing industry, such as: lack of infrastructure and
assigned land, environmental pollution, interference with non-fishing
activities, conflicting interest with other port users, etc. Moreover,
the port rehabilitation program supported by this project will also affect
these operations during and after construction. This situation requires
immediate attention, given the fast growth of fishing activities in the
Region.
Objectives. The main objective is to elaborate a plan to allow an orderly
and efficient development of the fishing industry in the Vth Region,
including physical as well as institutional matters.
Scope.  The study will include:   (i) a revision of the projections of
fishing activities in the area; (ii) definition of the required
infrastructure to satisfy the demand of artisan, semi-industrial, and
industrial fishing activities; (iii) an economic and social evaluation of
possible projects; (iv) recommendations of financing and operating schemes
of rhe projects by private groups;  and  (v) detailed or preliminary
engineering if financed by the Government or private groups, respectively.
Cost and Timina. The estimated cost, excluding taxes, is:
Consultants:  18 man-months x US$ 3,000           US$ 54,000
Travel and related expenses                       US$  6,000
Total                                             USS 60.000
The tentative chronogram will be:
Preparation of Terms of Reference           March 1992
Study Award                                 June 1992
Completion of the Study                     March 1993
Implementation                              April 1993

(v)   Libertador/Los Angeles Corridor

II. Training
1.    Project-related training would be addressed to high-level professional
staff of the following Government agencies: EMPORCHI, IIC, DOP and MINTRATEL.
These are the agencies most directly involved in port planning, financing,
construction, operation, administration, environmental control and maintenance,
and are also responsible for intermodal transport. The training program would
include the participation of professionals, referred to above, in courses,
international conferences and seminars, visits to terminals and ports, and
lectures given in Chile by experts with vast experience in port related matters.
The participation of managerial staff of private port and inland terminal
operators in the program should be encouraged, although loan funds allocated to
training will not cover expenses of private participants. A general training
program including objectives, scope, areas to be covered, beneficiaries,
selection criteria, and format of annual reports on training to be prepared
during project execution, was discussed and agreed with each agency, and related
documents are included in the Project File (Annex 10).
2.    In particular, the training activities of each agency will be primarily
addressed to the followingt   (i) EMPORCHIs the program will comprise the
following areas: planning, port operations, engineering, computer applications,
management of projects and financing. About thirty professionals will benefit
from the program, nine participating in international seminars and twenty-one
visiting areas of interest.   The total estimated amount woule be around
US$100,000; (ii) IICs the program will focus on the areas relevant to this
committee, such as: institutional aspects in the infrastructure sector, resource
allocation and planning for infrastructure, and supervision and coordtnation of
investment programs.   The program will  consist of two seminars  and two
conferences to be held in Santiago, courses, and related activities. The total
amount would be approximately US$100,000; (iii) DOP: the main areas of interest
will  be port  planning  aad engineering.    There will be  around  eighteen
professionals who will participate during project implementation, and the total



- 112 -
ANNEX 7
Page 12 of 12
estimated cost would be US$170,000; and (iv) MINTRATEL: the main areas of
interest will be port planning including physical and strategic planniaig, well-
balanced development of sea-land interface areas, environmental impact,
concession systems for port developments by private groups, multimodal transport,
and decentralization of port administration.   the total estimated coat will
amount to US$130,000.  In summary, the total estimated cost of the training
program would be: US$500.000.

CHILE
TRANSPORT INFRASTRUCTURE PROJECT
Port Operations
A. Current Situation
1.          A number of commercial ports in Chile are owned and administered by
EMPORCHI, the state-owned port enterprise; however, all cargo-handling serviceo
and related equipment,  except quay cranes,  are provided by   several port
operators who are supposed to compete among themselves, although only the larger
ones at each port actually do so. The container crane installed at Valparaiso,
however, is privately owned. Berth assignment is made by EMPORCHI at the ship
agent's request, and daily operations, including use of storage areas, are
coordinated by the enterprise together with the port operators and Customs.
Maritime services, namely, pilotage and towage are also provided by private
pilots and private towage companies, licensed by and under concessions awarded
by DIRECTEMAR, respectively. Container operations are carried out along the same
procedures, the exception being that in the case of Valparaiso containers may be
transferred directly from the ship side to a private, Customs-controlled,
container depot adjacent to the port.
B. Port Productivity
2.          As a result of the modernization of Chile's ports (1.11) productivity
and efficiency increased dramatically. The table below shows a comparison of
efficiency of the project ports with other ports in the world, expressed in
ton/ship/hour using the UNCTAD's Cargo Performance Index (CPI) corresponding to
the average rate based on total time ships occupying berths. The results are
clearly favorable to the project ports, except in containers where the
technological and physical improvements supported by the project would facilitate
a significant increase of the indicator.
COMPARISON OF PORT PRODUCTIVITY INDICATORS 1/
Commodity Group                                     Comparator Ports
San       San    Valpa-   Group I    Group II
Vicente   Antonio  raiso   Countries  Countries
Dry Bulk                   460       220      -       142          42
General Cargo              137       110     105       69          16
Fruit                       -         -      115     n.a.          n.a.
Containers                  -         24      32       60          41
1/ Comparison based on 1986 data for Groups I and II, corresponding to Developed
and Developing Countries, respectively; Chilean ports' indicators correspond to
1990 data.



- 114 -
Page 2 o' 3
C. Future Port Onerations
3.          Future port operations at the project ports is expected to be as
follows:
-     at San Viconte, the prevailing multiple port operator system, most
likely, will be maintained, at the same productivity levels as
today'al
-     at San Antonio, the Government has decided to follow the same
arrangement as at Valparaiso for the provision of cargo handling
services and equipment;
-     at Valparaiso,  the current concessionary  arrangements  for the
provision of cargo-handling services by multiple operators will
continue. The only container crane in this port was provided by the
biggest private port operator, and the terms of the concession
provide for the obligation to serve all vessels requiring the use of
the crane at established hourly rates. The Government has decided
that similar arrangements will be followed for the additional
cranes, but the concession for their provision would be awarded on
a competitive basis. The Chilean Maritime Chamber that represents
most of shipping lines, agents and port operators has already
expressed the interest of its members to provide the necessary
equipment.
4*          In addition to the above, the Exporters Association, representing
exclusively fruit exporters, is currently engaged in negotiations with the local
and foreign authorities responsible for the sanitary inspection, to improve the
existing procedures ,n such a way that this can take place in stations to be
established at strategically located sites closer to che production zones. If the
negotiations are successful, inspection of samples would not delay trucks
carrying the fruit to the ports, and the flow of trucks awaiting to be unloaded
at the ports would be facilitated.
5.          With regard to containerized cargo, LCL imports have still to clear
customs at the port of entry, the exception up to now being a private container
dopot adjacent to the port of Valparaiso controlled by customs. Current
regulations allow customs' clearance at inland depots located within the
municipality of the port of entTy, but none of the existing ones in the
Valparaiso Municipality has yet been staffed by customsl the reasons for the
above are, apparently, shortage of customs personnel and the additional cost that
this arrangement would cause to them. The Bank, throuah the Technical Assistance
Loan (Loan 2504-CH), is currently assisting customs to modernize the system. The
proposed project includes technical assistance for the establishment of inland
container depots closer to Santiago, final destination of the majority of
containerized cargo, where customs inspection and clearance can take place.
rI



- 115 -
ANNEX 8
Page 3 of 3
6.          Finally, an aspect that was considored in the economic evaluation of
the extension of the port of San Vicente, is that at present there are other
specialized private port facilities under construction that are designed
specifically to handle timber chips; this is expected to divert part of the chips
currently handled at San Vicente, liberating important port areas for more
efficient handling of other forestry products.
D. Small-scale Fishing Ports
7.          The construction of these kind of facilities is the responsibility
of DOP; but theii administration, operation and maintenance is ill-defined to say
the least. The proposed project would include a study to define the operational
requirements, users' charges, administrative arrangements that would have to be
established, and the economic and financial viability of the proposed investment
to carry out the small-scale fishing ports improvement program. Outline terms of
reference for this study are given in Annex 7.

CHILE
TRANSPORT INFRASTRUCTURE PROJECT
Port Environment Improvement - Plan of Action
Back&round
1.          Improvement of port environmental conditions is already in progress
at Valparaiso, where DIRECTEMAR has taken some measures to prevent pollution of
sea waters, particularly in the port areas, and the Government together with the
Municipality of Valparaiso are responsible for the execution of the Valparaiso
Water and Sewerage Project (Loan 3331-CH) financea by the Bank.  The plan of
action, which is based on the recommendations contained in the Environmental
Assessment of the p--4ect ports prepared by the NAEP of Denmark, is expected to
institutionalize compL2.ance with port environmental standards, and complement the
above mentioned ongoing measures.
Obiectives
2.    The objectives  of the plan are addressed to:  (a) prevent negative
environmental impact at the project ports during construction; (b) identify the
ports' needs to prevent and remedy environmental problems generated by ships
calling on them and bulk-handling (minerals) and storage, and take all necessary
measures to ensure that such needs are properly satisfied; and (c) compile
environmental port standards 1and regulations, including the port basins and
access channels that would have to be complied with by all port operators and
users.  The above regulations and standards will be implemented first at the
project ports and then gradually at all other public and private ports.
Actions to achieve the objectives. The plan would include, but not be limited
to:
(a)   during constructiont (i) the preparation of an analysis of the material to
be dredged at Valparaiso and San Antonio, to determine the degree of its
contamination from port and urban pollutants, and its suitability to be
used as land fill; (ii) analysis of the nature and characteeistics of
marine currents and sediment behavior in areas where dredged material will
be dumped; (iii) obtain and implement or have implemented municipal
regulations and restrictions, including enforcement and monitoring,
concerning transit of construction machinery and vehicles through urban
areas, disposal of demolition materials and any other activity generated
by the construction works that could have a negative environmental effect
in the urban and suburban areas; (iv) in case the analysis referred to in
para. (i) concludes that dredging is not suitable for land fill dredging
material would have to be disposed of farther than 12 miles from the coast
or at a depth deeper than 60 meters; and



- 117 -
ANNEX 9
Page 2 of 2
(b)   port operations-related actions:  (i) compile and make arrangements to
comply with port environmental standards and regulations; (ii) analyze
operating procedures of the fishing fleet, the fishing and chemical
industries for the handling and transport oi raw tmaterials, processed
products and waste, and define actions required to prevent and reduce
environmental damage; (iii) establish monitoring systems at San Antonio to
evaluate risks of mineral concentrates' dust affecting fruit exports or
any other food products; and at all project ports, procedures to mon tor
compliance by the fishing fleet and industries with environmental
standards and regulations; (iv) develop and implement specific plans at
the project ports to prevent, monitor, and combat environmentally
dangerous accidents; and (v) ensure that project ports are equipped to
receive and dispose of ships' waste.
Consultant services will be retained to prepare terms of reference of
technical assistance required to carry out the plan of action, as well as for
coordinating and monitoring its execution.
implementation Schedule
-  specifications satisfactory to the Bank will be included in the bidding
documents  for all major civil works  concerning disposal  of dredging and
demolition materials and traffic restrictions;
-  terms of reference for the technical assistance required to implement the
detailed plan of action to be completed not later than June 30, 1992;
-  studies to be completed and port standards to be compiled not later than
November 30, 1993;
- monitoring and implementation of the consultants' recommendations not later
than December 30, 1993.
Long-term Ob ectives
3.    All  other environmental problems  generated by  the cities'  sewerage
discharge into the sea and particularly in the ports and harbors are expected to
be dealt with through a separate proCram that would include treatment plants,
submarine sewerage emissaries, etc. Limits and restrictions for the disposal of
industrial waste in port areas would be defined based on standards to be compiled
and implemented during the project.
